National Education Achievement Exhibition to be Held Before the Double Tenth Festival 255

The Ministry of Education Has Drafted Regulations

The Exhibition Will Last for Three Weeks

(Nanjing, 19th) The Ministry of Education has decided to hold a National Education Achievement Exhibition in the capital before the Double Tenth Festival. The exhibition will last for three weeks. The draft regulations have been drafted by the Social Education Department and will be submitted for approval before a committee is formed to prepare everything.

Ministry of Education Promulgates 256

Regulations for Primary and Secondary Schools, Normal Schools, and Vocational Schools (I)

Based on the Law on Primary and Secondary Schools, Normal Schools, and Vocational Schools passed by the Legislative Yuan, and in order to provide a basis for those running schools, the Ministry of Education, through its Department of General Education and the Counselor's Office, has compiled four types of regulations for primary schools, secondary schools, normal schools, and vocational schools. This took two months, with more than ten ministry meetings and dozens of group meetings held successively. After repeated revisions and reviews, and to expedite the promulgation, the organizers worked day and night. Finally, on the 18th, the review of the four types of regulations was completed and officially promulgated on the same day. However, sending them to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities will take some time after they have been typeset and printed. The four types of regulations are recorded below.

(I) Primary School Regulations 257

Chapter 1 General Principles

Article 1 These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 17 of the Primary School Law.

Article 2 Primary schools are places for the implementation of national compulsory education. According to the provisions of Article 1 of the Primary School Law, the following training shall be implemented: (1) Cultivating children's healthy physique, (2) Tempering children's good character, (3) Developing children's aesthetic interests, (4) Enhancing children's life skills, (5) Training children's labor habits, (6) Enlightening children's scientific thinking, (7) Cultivating children's spirit of mutual assistance and unity, (8) Developing children's concept of patriotism and love for the community.

Article 3 Primary schools accept school-age children for a period of six years. Before education is universal, a period of four years will be considered the end of compulsory education.

Article 4 Primary schools are divided into two levels. The first four years are the junior primary school, which may be established independently. The last two years are the senior primary school, which must be established in conjunction with the junior primary school.

Article 5 In order to promote compulsory education, in addition to the above-mentioned primary schools, simple primary schools and short-term primary schools may be established in various localities. Simple primary schools enroll school-age children who cannot enter junior primary schools, and their study period is calculated by converting teaching time to 6,2800 hours. Short-term primary schools enroll older out-of-school children aged 10 to 16, and their study period is one year, calculated by converting teaching time to at least 540 hours. Simple primary schools and short-term primary schools shall be operated in accordance with the Ministry of Education's Implementation Measures for the First Phase of Compulsory Education and Implementation Measures for Short-Term Compulsory Education.

Chapter 2 Establishment and Management 258

Article 6 Primary schools are established in accordance with the provisions of Articles 3, 4, and 5 of the Primary School Law.

Article 7 Each county and city, in order to promote the establishment of primary schools and facilitate management, should use autonomous regions as school districts. When an autonomous region is too large, it may be divided into two or three school districts.

Article 8 Primary schools established by the province are called provincial primary schools.

Article 9 The affiliated primary school of a normal school, in addition to providing practice for normal school students, has the same nature as an independent primary school.

Article 10 Primary schools established by provinces and cities for the purpose of testing educational methods are called provincial or municipal experimental primary schools.

Article 11 Provincial primary schools are named after the place where they are located. Public primary schools below the county and city level are named after smaller areas. If there are two or more public primary schools in one place with the same name, they may be distinguished by the order of numbers. Private primary schools should use proper names and may not use place names as school names.

Article 12 Primary schools are managed by educational administrative organs at all levels. The scope is as follows: (1) Provincial primary schools are under the jurisdiction of the provincial education department. (2) Municipal primary schools and private primary schools in the city are under the jurisdiction of the municipal education administrative organ. (3) Primary schools established in counties, districts, townships, and towns, as well as private primary schools within the county, are under the jurisdiction of the county education administrative organ.

Article 13 The establishment, alteration, and closure of primary schools must be reported to the主管 educational administrative organ for approval and record.

Article 14 Primary schools specially established by agencies other than the educational administrative organ are supervised and guided by the local主管 educational administrative organ.

Article 15 Within one month after the beginning of each semester, primary schools should submit to the主管 educational administrative organ for approval and record the overall situation of the school organization, the grade composition, the roster of teachers and staff, the roster of children, etc.

Article 16 Within two months after the beginning of each semester, provincial primary schools and affiliated primary schools of national colleges and universities above the junior college level should report the roster of children for the current semester, the roster of graduating children for the previous semester, etc., to the local county and city educational administrative organ for record.

Article 17 Experimental primary schools should submit the experimental plan and results to the主管 educational administrative organ and forward them to the Ministry of Education for approval and record.

Article 18 People who are not citizens of the Republic of China or their organized groups may not establish primary schools for educating Chinese children within the territory of the Republic of China.

Article 19 The establishment of private primary schools shall be governed by the regulations on private schools in addition to the provisions of the Primary School Law and these regulations.

Chapter 3 Funding 259

Article 20 The ratio of school building and equipment to the opening expenses of a primary school should be 66:47:3.

Article 21 The distribution of primary school recurring expenses should be based on the following percentages in principle: Salaries of teachers and staff, approximately 70%; expenses for books, instruments, sports equipment, and teaching equipment, approximately 15%; expenses for experiments, stationery, utilities, etc., approximately 9%; expenses for travel, insurance, and special expenses, approximately 3%; reserve fund, approximately 3%. The aforementioned reserve fund may not be used without the approval of the主管 educational administrative organ.

Article 22 The standard for primary school funding shall be formulated by the educational administrative organs of each province and city and submitted to the Ministry of Education for record and implementation.

Article 23 The expenditure of primary school funds should strive for frugality and accuracy. The measures for public review, etc., shall be formulated by the educational administrative organs of each province and city and reported to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation.

Chapter 4 Staffing 260

Article 24 Primary school schools should compile and assign students based on their age and ability when they enroll.

Article 25 The staffing of primary schools shall be in accordance with the provisions of Article 7 of the Primary School Law. The number of students per class shall be 40, with a minimum of 25.

Zhejiang University President Guo's Plan 261

Guo Renyuan, the new president of Zhejiang University, convened all faculty, staff, and students on the 17th for a speech, mainly covering the following points: (1) After the administrative unification of Zhejiang, further work should be done to improve the efficiency of administration. (2) In reorganizing finances, the first step should be to check whether there is any internal waste in the school. (3) The school should focus on academic affairs, with the administrative part only assisting academic affairs. (4) It is advocated to vigorously save on administrative expenses and use the funds specifically to increase library equipment for the three colleges. (5) Equal importance should be attached to the development of the three colleges, and it is advocated that the academic affairs of the three colleges should have considerable connections. (6) For each department, it is advocated to enrich the content and narrow the scope. Mr. Guo estimates that after vigorous tightening of administrative expenses, at least 40,000 yuan can be saved each year, and he is determined to keep this amount for the equipment of the three colleges, so the equipment of the three colleges should be considerable. Mr. Guo also announced yesterday that the administration will be reorganized. The original administrative organization of Zhejiang University was the Secretariat, with one Secretary-General and two secretaries, divided into six sections: document registration, administrative affairs, accounting, library, and publishing. Each section had one section chief and several section members and assistants. There were also student life instructors, a school doctor's office, a military training department, and a physical education department, all directly under the president. Now, President Guo has reorganized the Secretariat into the Secretariat and the General Affairs Office. The Secretariat has five sections: document registration, library, military training, and physical education (the original publishing section has been canceled). The General Affairs Office has two sections: administrative affairs, accounting, and medical affairs. The title of Secretary-General Jiang is canceled, and the original two secretaries are reduced to one. Also, student life instructors have been dismissed. In this way, monthly expenses can be saved. It is said that Wang Shiying has been internally appointed as the secretary, and Tong Dingzhi has been hired as the director of general affairs.

Report on the Ministry of Education Inspector's Inspection of Education in Shanxi Province 262

(8) Existing middle schools should be reorganized or eliminated, taking into account the suitability of the region and the needs of society. More joint middle schools should be established, and efforts should be made to make them co-educational, add high schools, enrich the content, improve the treatment of teachers, and hire more full-time teachers to assist the principal in managing administrative and educational affairs.

(9) Existing normal schools should be greatly reformed. Male and female schools should be merged, and three to five schools should be set up in key areas. The rest can be moved to rural areas or reorganized into joint normal schools. It is also advisable to weigh the urgency and gradually increase them. The system of free subsidies for normal school students must be restored, but the subsidies can be appropriately reduced compared to the previous amount. The curriculum should focus on practice and also take into account the characteristics of rural education.

(10) Junior vocational schools must be carefully planned and completed within a time limit. Senior vocational schools should add various specialized schools as needed by the local area, and the internship equipment must be complete.

(11) Compulsory education should be promoted quickly, and short-term compulsory education is especially important. The Taiyuan City experimental zone has just been established. The results of its operation and the effect of urging various counties to comply should be strictly reviewed and reported by the department.

(12) Senior primary schools should be co-educational. The level should be raised uniformly to connect with junior high schools. Special attention should be paid to the授與 of production skills and the cultivation of labor habits. Efforts should be made to popularize junior primary schools. In remote areas, joint primary schools should be established by combining two or more districts, neighborhoods, townships, and towns. In single-grade or two-part schools, the grouping teaching must be匀称 and appropriate. Poor children who cannot afford to buy textbooks and educational supplies should be provided with them.

(13) Among schools at all levels, those with unstable school buildings that are in danger of collapsing and those with cramped classrooms that cannot accommodate students, although few, should be repaired and expanded separately. Facilities such as libraries, gyms, and bathrooms should also be emphasized. The complexity of the equipment in internship places, such as factories and farms, should depend on the nature of the school and the needs of the environment.

(14) Teaching equipment in schools at all levels, such as reference books, specimens, and instruments, should be added as much as possible according to the needs of the school, and the quantity should be enriched. The quality should be new, and the original equipment should also be diligently organized. Colleges and universities are large in scale and should be complete. Other things, such as extracurricular reading materials that are not closely related to coursework, can be purchased later.

(15) The curriculum for schools at all levels must be based on educational principles and the nature of the subjects, with the general rules of rich content, novel teaching materials, appropriate level, organized structure, and clear outline, and the curriculum should be revised. Primary and secondary schools should implement teaching in accordance with the standards set by the Ministry, and primary schools can appropriately add rural teaching materials.

(16) Teaching in schools at all levels must be based on the nature of the subjects and the psychology of the students, and the most economical and effective methods should be adopted separately. The method of injection, which is detrimental to the development of the spirit, should not be used unilaterally, especially in primary schools. Teachers should be responsible for guiding self-study and extracurricular reading. The graduation examinations for primary and secondary school students should be implemented quickly, and the review of the middle school entrance examination papers can continue to be carried out.

(17) The moral education of schools at all levels should be implemented conscientiously in accordance with the training objectives set by the Ministry. In strict training, the meaning of personality influence should be used to疏导 their thoughts, regulate their lives, patiently guide them, and be moderate in宽严, in order to achieve the practical effect of cultivating good character and整饬风纪. Teachers should be responsible for guidance, and there should not be excessive setting up of moral education personnel.

(18) Physical education in schools at all levels should be carried out in accordance with the Ministry's orders. Physical education committees should be established quickly, standards should be set, and progress should be strictly supervised. Those with incomplete equipment must do their best to expand it. Health should be properly guided by the school doctor, and schools without a school doctor can be responsible by the teachers.

(19) The implementation of various social education facilities should be筹办 in accordance with the three important facilities for promoting social education, namely, the promotion of mass schools must be督促 to realize it as scheduled, and the exhibition department of the mass education hall must be迅予改组成立. In addition, the affairs of various departments must also be completed in the shortest period of time. Libraries, newspaper offices, mobile libraries, public sports fields, recreation fields, literacy campaigns, popular lectures, remedial education, special education, social education personnel training institutes, and other undertakings should be separately整顿 and兴办 as soon as possible.

(20) The preservation of antiquities should be切实 responsible by the antiquities preservation committees of each county to avoid destruction. In areas where antiquities are more prevalent, such as Datong County, a larger preservation committee should be organized to manage them. If necessary, the power of the state can be used to help it proceed.

Local 263

Shanghai University Faculty Association Established Yesterday 264

Elected Executive Committee Members: Chu Minyi, etc. Supervisory Committee Members: Zheng Hongnian, etc.

Nationwide Education Sector Mobilized to Resist Japan from April 1st

The Shanghai University Faculty and Staff Federation, which has been preparing for more than a year, held its first membership meeting at 12:00 noon yesterday on the 9th floor of the YMCA in Eight Immortals Bridge and was officially established. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Members 265

Including members from various universities such as Chih Tze, Tongji, Chung Kung, Soochow, Chinan, Fudan, Labor University, Kiangnan, Wen Hua, Merchant Marine, Great China, Cheng Feng, Aurora, Great Tong, New Chung Kung, Business School, Medical School, and Franco-Chinese Institute of Technology: Ouyang, Jiang Zhensan, Zhong Hangsu, Kang Xuanyi, Xu Zeyi, Yan Kechang, Zhuang Qunhui, Yang Bingxun, Long Tiyao, Zhang Shouyong, Hu Qibing, Hu Puan, Ma Gongyu, Li Quanshi, Zhou Xinmin, Luo Aisi, Zhang Jixin, Yu Zhongbiao, Lin Zhongke, Song Chongjiu, etc., more than seventy people.

Establishment Situation: At 12:00, all members held a lunch, and the meeting was opened at 1:00. Chairman Zhang Shouyong and recorder Yang Bingxun performed the rituals. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, and the preparatory committee member Lin Zhongke reported the preparation process. Then, the constitution was amended, and the foundation and supervisory committee members were elected. Proposals were discussed, and the meeting was adjourned at about 5:00 pm for a photo.

Preparation Process: Lin Zhongke reported the preparation process, saying roughly that the association convened the inaugural meeting on December 16, 1931, and elected the preparatory committee members to organize the preparatory committee. The preparatory committee convened six meetings successively. It was originally planned to be prepared and established in February of last year, but the members were scattered due to the January 28th war, and it was impossible to convene the meeting. The studio was suspended for a year. Now, with the national crisis becoming increasingly urgent, it is necessary for people in the education sector to unite, so the sixth preparatory committee decided to establish it today on the 12th of this month.

Amendment of the Constitution: Jiang Zhensan, Kang Xuanyi, Chu Minyi, and 32 others proposed to amend the constitution: (A) Principles: (1) Abolish the Congress of Representatives; (2) The Executive and Supervisory Committees should be directly elected by the General Assembly of Members; (3) Increase the number of Executive and Supervisory Committee members; (B) Articles: (1) The articles of the original constitution relating to the Congress of Representatives, such as Article (4), Item (B), Article (5) in its entirety, and Article (10) Item (C), should be deleted; (2) The original text of Article 6 stated that the Executive Committee of this Association shall consist of fifteen members and the Supervisory Committee shall consist of five members, who shall be elected by the Congress of Representatives and shall not be limited to representatives, with a term of one year, should be changed to (the Executive Committee of this Association shall consist of thirty-one members, with seven alternates, and the Supervisory Committee shall consist of seven members, with three alternates, who shall be elected by the General Assembly of Members, with a term of one year, and may be re-elected for consecutive terms); (3) Seven members of the Executive Committee shall be mutually elected as Standing Members to handle daily affairs. It was immediately resolved and passed according to the proposal.

Important Anti-Japanese Proposals: Xu Zeyi, Zhong Hangsu, Zhang Shouyong, Hu Puan, and 46 others proposed four important anti-Japanese proposals, all of which were passed by the entire body. The original proposals were as follows: (1) To call on the whole country to revive the movement to boycott Japanese goods; (2) To send a telegram to the whole country stating that no peace treaty should be signed with Japan before the Northeast is recovered, urging the government to use the country's entire military force to save the Northeast, and that anyone who violates this purpose should be regarded as an enemy of the whole country; (3) To call on the entire education sector to mobilize nationwide to resist Japanese aggression from April 1st; (4) To ask the central government to earnestly send troops to aid and fully supply the Song and Sun armies in resisting Japan.

New Executive and Supervisory Committee Members: (1) Executive Committee: Kang Xuanyi, Zhang Shouyong, Lin Zhongke, Wang Xiaotong, Jiang Zhensan, Li Quanshi, Chu Minyi, Zhu Zhangbao, Zhang Jixin, Xu Zeyi, Qiu Hanping, Zhong Hangsu, Wu Zijing, Song Chongjiu, Wang Yuzhang, Wang Xiaowen, Liao Songxue, Chen Jilie, Lei Guoneng, Chen Zhenlu, Cui Xiaocen, Ge Shihua, Hu Puan, Sun Yue, Zhang Junqi, Li Shengwu, Zhou Manfan, Chen Qifu, Long Tiyao, He Ziheng, Zhang Shilu, etc., thirty-one people; (2) Alternate Executive Committee Members: Li Yongzhong, Sun Boqian, Xi Yushu, Huang Xianzhang, Yu Shaowu, Meng Shouchun, Cai Zhenghua, etc., seven people; (3) Supervisory Committee Members: Zheng Hongnian, Li Denghui, Weng Zhilong, Chu Fucheng, He Shizhen, Shen Junru, Yan Fuqing, etc., seven people; (4) Alternate Supervisory Committee Members: Ou Yuanhuai, Hu Qibing, Liu Zhanen, etc., three people.

Convening of the Standing Committee: After the election, the elected Executive Committee members convened a temporary meeting and decided to hold the first standing committee meeting next week. Kang Xuanyi was elected to convene the meeting, and the date will be determined by Kang Xuanyi and notified separately by letter. Then, Committee Member Kang told the Shanghai News reporter that the association's meeting place will be temporarily borrowed from the YMCA in Eight Immortals Bridge until a suitable place is found.

Municipal Education Bureau Sends Personnel 266

To Investigate the Situation of Memorial Weeks in Various Schools

Personnel Will Also Be Sent to Participate When Necessary

The Municipal Education Bureau of this city believes that the Memorial Week of Dr. Sun Yat-sen held by various schools every Monday is stipulated by the central government and must not be neglected. However, recently, some schools have not earnestly complied with it, which is a violation of the law. Therefore, the bureau has sent personnel to various schools to investigate the situation of holding Memorial Week. When necessary, personnel will also be sent to participate and give speeches in various schools to promote it.

Municipal Education Hall Prepares 267

Children's Living Guidance Exhibition

Children's Table Tennis Competition Expands Quota

Preliminary Rounds Scheduled to Begin on the 25th of This Month

The Shanghai Municipal Public Education Hall, in order to promote children's education and enlighten children's knowledge, is now preparing a children's living guidance exhibition, which will be opened on this year's Children's Day. The content will include models and charts on children's clothing, food, and housing, as well as children's utensils and various gifts that are in line with educational meaning. In addition, the children's table tennis competition prepared by the hall started registration on March 1st. Now, in order to increase children's interest in the competition, the quota has been increased by 60 places, and the preliminary rounds are scheduled to be held at 1:00 pm on the 25th of this month and at 10:00 am on the 26th. The date of the finals will be on April 5th.

Wang Jiyuan's Art Exhibition Closes Tonight 268

Yesterday's Attendance Was the Highest

Scheduled to Close at 8:00 PM Tonight

The solo art exhibition of famous painter Wang Jiyuan had the highest attendance of Chinese and Western people yesterday. All the works are Wang's creations after returning from his European tour. His oil paintings, watercolors, water-based paintings, and fruit paintings are all superb. It is scheduled to close at 8:00 pm tonight. It is estimated that fifteen of Wang's works have been collected by Chinese and Western people. His style has a great and profound influence on the general youth. Foreigners who love literature and art have praised him endlessly.

Nanyang Information, Issue 7, Compiled and Published by Jinan University's Cultural Department 269

Since the publication of the Nanyang Information bi-monthly magazine published by the Nanyang and American Cultural Affairs Department of National Jinan University, it has been well received by people from all walks of life at home and abroad because of its精新 content and rich materials. Not only can it be read as news, but the materials in it can also be used as important references. More than a dozen people come every day to request exchanges and subscriptions. The seventh issue has been published a few days ago, and the length has increased and the content is richer than the previous issues. It includes Chen Qiying's "One more word to the Ministry of Communications that wants to increase the postage in Nanyang" ("Points to note when unifying the collection of donations from overseas Chinese"), Jiang Yingliang's "(The current crisis of overseas Chinese education in Nanyang)", Su Hongbin's "Revision of the Divorce Rules in the Straits Colonies," Chen Xiweng's "The Decline of the Malayan Economy in 1932," Chen Gangfu's "(The mutiny in the Dutch East Indies)", Ye Shaochun's "(The relationship between Nanyang and the Chao-Mei people)", Wang Weisi's "(The handicraft industry of the gentry in the Malay Peninsula)", Hu Weihan's "(Overview of the Cuban Chinese)", Liu Shimu's "(Nanyang Anecdotes)", Zhou Tingzhen's "The Death of Xiao Xin'an", Hu Juegen's "(Walking around the Dingjia Lang area)", and dozens of sections on overseas Chinese affairs, overseas Chinese conditions, and important news from Nanyang. In order to popularize it, the price of the newspaper is extremely low. A full year of twenty issues only costs a total of one yuan and two angles for postage, and in order to give preferential treatment to overseas Chinese schools, newspapers, and groups, whether subscribing for half a year or a full year, only postage is charged.
